The [2020 Stadium Series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NHL_Stadium_Series "2020 NHL Stadium Series") saw the Kings wear special black and white uniforms with "LA" tilted upward in front, along with chrome helmets. The uniforms took cues from the angular architecture and aircraft of the [United States Air Force Academy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy "United States Air Force Academy").[\[111\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-112)

In the 2020–21 season, the Kings unveiled a "Reverse Retro" alternate uniform in collaboration with Adidas. The uniform essentially recreated the design worn from 1988 to 1998, but black and silver were replaced by the team's original purple and gold colors.[\[112\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-113)

Before the 2021–22 season, the Kings replaced their silver alternates with a modernized version of the throwback 1990s white uniforms. The design featured slightly different striping patterns from the originals, and were paired with chrome helmets.[\[113\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-114) In the [2024 Stanley Cup playoffs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Stanley_Cup_playoffs "2024 Stanley Cup playoffs"), the Kings opted to wear these alternates during road games, but replaced the chrome helmets with the primary white helmets.[\[114\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-115)

A second "Reverse Retro" uniform was unveiled in the 2022–23 season, featuring the 1980–88 uniform but with a white base, purple stripes and gold accents.[\[115\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-116)

On June 20, 2024, the Kings unveiled a new primary logo, which is a modernized version of their 1988 logo.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-LAKingsBrandEvolution-1) The new uniforms were also heavily based on the 1988–1998 uniforms, but the sleeve numbers were no longer placed on the contrasting stripe as they were in the previous uniform.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-117)

On October 7, 2025, the Kings released a new alternate uniform, using a black base and silver elements. The crest in front is the team's classic "crown" logo, and the fonts used were based on the wordmark found on the primary logo. The design was highly influenced by the original purple and gold "crown" uniforms the team wore from 1967 to 1980. Like with their previous alternate uniform, these were paired with chrome helmets, though on a few occasions they also wore the black helmets.[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-118)

### Mascot

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Mascot")\]

Since 2007, the mascot of the Kings is Bailey, a lion who wears No. 72 (the average temperature in Los Angeles). He was named in honor of [Garnet "Ace" Bailey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garnet_Bailey "Garnet Bailey"),[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-119) who served as Director of Pro Scouting for seven years before dying in the [September 11, 2001, terrorist attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks "September 11 attacks").[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-120) Bailey is the second mascot, after Kingston the [snow leopard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snow_leopard "Snow leopard") in the early 1990s, who now serves as the mascot of the Kings' AHL affiliate, the [Ontario Reign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontario_Reign "Ontario Reign").

## Rivalries

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Rivalries")\]

The Kings have developed strong rivalries with the two other Californian teams of the NHL,[\[120\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-outside-121) the [Anaheim Ducks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anaheim_Ducks "Anaheim Ducks") – who also play in the [Los Angeles metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area "Los Angeles metropolitan area"), leading to the rivalry dubbed the " [Freeway Face-Off](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freeway_Face-Off "Freeway Face-Off")" as both cities are separated by the [Interstate 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_5 "Interstate 5"),[\[121\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-122)[\[122\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-123) and the [rivalry with the San Jose Sharks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kings-Sharks_rivalry "Kings-Sharks rivalry") – also reflects the animosity between [Northern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_California "Northern California") and [Southern California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California").[\[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-124) The Kings eliminated both teams during the [2014 Stanley Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Stanley_Cup_playoffs "2014 Stanley Cup playoffs") run, and have played outdoor games with them for the [NHL Stadium Series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NHL_Stadium_Series "NHL Stadium Series"), losing to the Ducks at [Dodger Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodger_Stadium "Dodger Stadium") in 2014 and beating the Sharks at [Levi's Stadium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levi%27s_Stadium "Levi's Stadium") the following year.[\[120\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-outside-121) During the 1980s, the Kings developed a heated [rivalry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kings%E2%80%93Oilers_rivalry "Kings–Oilers rivalry") with the [Edmonton Oilers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmonton_Oilers "Edmonton Oilers"), which has rekindled in recent years after meeting and losing for four straight years in the first round of the playoffs against the Oilers between 2022 and 2025.[\[124\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-125)

### Team captains

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Team captains")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/An%C5%BEe_Kopitar_%2825992321104%29.jpg/250px-An%C5%BEe_Kopitar_%2825992321104%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:An%C5%BEe_Kopitar_(25992321104).jpg) Anze Kopitar served as the team's captain from 2016 to 2026.

Further information on team captains in ice hockey: [Captain (ice hockey)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Captain_(ice_hockey) "Captain (ice hockey)")

- [Bob Wall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Wall_(ice_hockey) "Bob Wall (ice hockey)"), 1967–1969
- [Larry Cahan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Cahan "Larry Cahan"), 1969–1971
- [Bob Pulford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Pulford "Bob Pulford"), 1971–1973
- [Terry Harper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Harper "Terry Harper"), 1973–1975
- [Mike Murphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Murphy_(ice_hockey,_born_1950) "Mike Murphy (ice hockey, born 1950)"), 1975–1981
- [Dave Lewis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Lewis_(ice_hockey) "Dave Lewis (ice hockey)"), 1981–1983
- [Terry Ruskowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Ruskowski "Terry Ruskowski"), 1983–1985
- [Dave Taylor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Taylor_(ice_hockey) "Dave Taylor (ice hockey)"), 1985–1989
- [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 1989–1996
- [Luc Robitaille](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luc_Robitaille "Luc Robitaille"), 1992–1993, 2006[\[128\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-RobitailleCaptain-129)
- [Rob Blake](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rob_Blake "Rob Blake"), 1996–2001, 2007–2008
- [Mattias Norstrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mattias_Norstrom "Mattias Norstrom"), 2001–2007
- [Dustin Brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dustin_Brown_(ice_hockey) "Dustin Brown (ice hockey)"), 2008–2016, 2022[\[129\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-BrownCaptain-130)
- [Anze Kopitar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/An%C5%BEe_Kopitar "Anže Kopitar"), 2016–2026[\[130\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-131)

### Head coaches

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Head coaches")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Darryl_Sutter_-_June_2014.jpg/250px-Darryl_Sutter_-_June_2014.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Darryl_Sutter_-_June_2014.jpg) [Darryl Sutter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darryl_Sutter "Darryl Sutter") was the head coach of the Kings from 2011 to 2017.

- [Red Kelly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Kelly "Red Kelly"): 1967–1969
- [Hal Laycoe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hal_Laycoe "Hal Laycoe"): 1969–1970
- [Johnny Wilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnny_Wilson_(ice_hockey) "Johnny Wilson (ice hockey)"): 1969–1970
- [Larry Regan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Regan "Larry Regan"): 1970–1972
- [Fred Glover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fred_Glover_(ice_hockey) "Fred Glover (ice hockey)"): 1971–1972
- [Bob Pulford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Pulford "Bob Pulford"): 1972–1977
- [Ron Stewart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Stewart "Ron Stewart"): 1977–1978
- [Bob Berry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Berry_(ice_hockey) "Bob Berry (ice hockey)"): 1978–1981
- [Parker MacDonald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parker_MacDonald "Parker MacDonald"): 1981–1982
- [Don Perry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don_Perry "Don Perry"): 1982–1984
- [Rogie Vachon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rogie_Vachon "Rogie Vachon") (interim):1 1984, 1988, 1995
- [Roger Neilson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Neilson "Roger Neilson"): 1984
- [Pat Quinn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Quinn_(ice_hockey) "Pat Quinn (ice hockey)"): 1984–1987
- [Mike Murphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Murphy_(ice_hockey,_born_1950) "Mike Murphy (ice hockey, born 1950)"): 1987–1988
- [Robbie Ftorek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robbie_Ftorek "Robbie Ftorek"): 1988–1989
- [Tom Webster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Webster_(ice_hockey) "Tom Webster (ice hockey)"): 1989–1992
- [Barry Melrose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barry_Melrose "Barry Melrose"): 1992–1995
- [Larry Robinson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Robinson "Larry Robinson"): 1995–1999
- [Andy Murray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andy_Murray_(ice_hockey) "Andy Murray (ice hockey)"): 1999–2006
- [John Torchetti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Torchetti "John Torchetti") (interim):2 2006
- [Marc Crawford](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_Crawford "Marc Crawford"): 2006–2008
- [Terry Murray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terry_Murray "Terry Murray"): 2008–2011
- [John Stevens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Stevens_(ice_hockey) "John Stevens (ice hockey)") (interim):3 2011, 2017–2018
- [Darryl Sutter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Darryl_Sutter "Darryl Sutter"): 2011–2017
- [Willie Desjardins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willie_Desjardins "Willie Desjardins"): (interim): 2018–2019
- [Todd McLellan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Todd_McLellan "Todd McLellan"): 2019–2024
- [Jim Hiller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Hiller "Jim Hiller"): 2024–2026[\[91\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-Hiller20241-92)[\[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-Hiller20242-93)
- [D. J. Smith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D._J._Smith_(ice_hockey) "D. J. Smith (ice hockey)"): 2026–present[\[99\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-Smith2026-100)

**Notes:**

- 1 Rogie Vachon took over as interim head coach for the Kings on three occasions, the first for two games in the middle of the 1983–84 season after Don Perry was fired, then replaced by Roger Neilson.[\[131\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-132)[\[132\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-133) The second time was for one game in the middle of 1987–88 season after Mike Murphy was fired, then replaced by Robbie Ftorek.[\[133\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-134) The third occasion was for the final seven games in the 1994–95 lockout-shortened season after Barry Melrose was fired, then replaced by Larry Robinson.[\[134\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-135) In all those times, he returned to his duties in the Kings front office.[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-136)
- 2 John Torchetti took over as interim head coach for the final 12 games of the 2005–06 season after Andy Murray was fired.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:0-137) Torchetti was replaced by Marc Crawford at the end of the 2005–06 season.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:0-137)
- 3 John Stevens took over as interim head coach for four games in the middle of the 2011–12 season after Terry Murray was fired.[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:1-138) He would return to his duties as assistant coach after Darryl Sutter was hired.[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:1-138) Stevens would return again, this time as the permanent replacement for Sutter in 2017.[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:1-138)

### Hall of Fame

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Hall of Fame")\]

The Los Angeles Kings acknowledge an affiliation with a number of inductees to the [Hockey Hall of Fame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hockey_Hall_of_Fame "Hockey Hall of Fame"), including 19 former players (five of whom earned their credentials primarily as Kings) and three builders of the sport.[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-medgu-148) The three individuals recognized as builders by the Hall of Fame includes former Kings head coaches, and general managers. In addition to players and builders, athletic trainers have been inducted into the Hall of Fame through the Professional Hockey Athletic Trainers Society, and the Society of Professional Hockey Equipment Managers.[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-train-149) Two athletic trainers from the Kings organization were inducted into the Hall of Fame: [Peter Demers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Demers "Peter Demers") in 2007 and Mark O'Neill in 2016.[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-medgu-148)[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-train-149)

Three [sports broadcasters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_broadcasting "Sports broadcasting") for the Kings were awarded the [Foster Hewitt Memorial Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foster_Hewitt_Memorial_Award "Foster Hewitt Memorial Award") for their contributions to hockey broadcasting: [Jiggs McDonald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jiggs_McDonald "Jiggs McDonald") (1990), [Bob Miller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Miller_(sportscaster) "Bob Miller (sportscaster)") (2000), and [Nick Nickson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Nickson "Nick Nickson") (2015).[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-medgu-148)[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-FosHA-150) In 2005, [Helene Elliott](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helene_Elliott "Helene Elliott"), a [sportswriter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sportswriter "Sportswriter") for the _[Los Angeles Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times "Los Angeles Times")_ was awarded the [Elmer Ferguson Memorial Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elmer_Ferguson_Memorial_Award "Elmer Ferguson Memorial Award") for her contributions to sports journalism.[\[149\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-151)

### Franchise records

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Franchise records")\]

#### Regular season scoring leaders

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Regular season scoring leaders")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/LucRobitaille.jpg/250px-LucRobitaille.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LucRobitaille.jpg) Luc Robitaille is the franchise's all-time leader in goals scored with 557.

These are the top-ten regular season scorers in franchise history.[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-152) Figures are updated after each completed NHL regular season.

-  \*  – current Kings player

_**Note:** Pos = Position; GP = Games played; G = Goals; A = Assists; Pts = Points; P/G = Points per game_

| Player | Pos | GP | G | A | Pts | P/G |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Anze Kopitar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/An%C5%BEe_Kopitar "Anže Kopitar") | C | 1,521 | 452 | 864 | **1,316** | .87 |
| [Marcel Dionne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcel_Dionne "Marcel Dionne") | C | 921 | 550 | 757 | **1,307** | 1.42 |
| [Luc Robitaille](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luc_Robitaille "Luc Robitaille") | LW | 1,079 | 557 | 597 | **1,154** | 1.07 |
| [Dave Taylor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Taylor_(ice_hockey) "Dave Taylor (ice hockey)") | RW | 1,111 | 431 | 638 | **1,069** | .96 |

Shutouts

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Jonathan_Quick.jpg/250px-Jonathan_Quick.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jonathan_Quick.jpg) Recording 10 shutouts during the [2011–12 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season "2011–12 NHL season"), [Jonathan Quick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Quick "Jonathan Quick") holds the franchise record for most shutouts in a season.Regular season records

- Most goals: [Bernie Nicholls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernie_Nicholls "Bernie Nicholls"), 70 ( [1988–89](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_NHL_season "1988–89 NHL season"))
- Most assists: [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 122 ( [1990–91](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_NHL_season "1990–91 NHL season"))
- Most points: [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 168 (1988–89)
- Most points in a game: [Bernie Nicholls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernie_Nicholls "Bernie Nicholls"), 8 (1988–89)
- Most penalty minutes: [Marty McSorley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marty_McSorley "Marty McSorley"), 399 ( [1992–93](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_NHL_season "1992–93 NHL season"))
- Most points, defenseman: [Larry Murphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Murphy_(ice_hockey) "Larry Murphy (ice hockey)"), 76 ( [1980–81](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_NHL_season "1980–81 NHL season"))
- Most points, rookie: [Luc Robitaille](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luc_Robitaille "Luc Robitaille"), 84 ( [1986–87](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_NHL_season "1986–87 NHL season"))
- Most wins: [Jonathan Quick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Quick "Jonathan Quick"), 40 ( [2015–16](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_NHL_season "2015–16 NHL season"))
- Most shutouts: [Jonathan Quick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Quick "Jonathan Quick"), 10 ( [2011–12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NHL_season "2011–12 NHL season"))

Playoff records

- Most goals: [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 15 (1992–93)
- Most assists: [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 25 (1992–93)
- Most points: [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 40 (1992–93)
- Most points in a game: [Tomas Sandstrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomas_Sandstr%C3%B6m "Tomas Sandström"), [Tony Granato](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Granato "Tony Granato"), [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky"), 5 ( [1989–90](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_NHL_season "1989–90 NHL season"))
- Most penalty minutes: [Jay Miller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jay_Miller_(ice_hockey) "Jay Miller (ice hockey)"), 63 (1988–89)
- Most points, defenseman: [Drew Doughty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drew_Doughty "Drew Doughty"), 18 ( [2013–14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_NHL_season "2013–14 NHL season"))
- Most points, rookie: [Tyler Toffoli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyler_Toffoli "Tyler Toffoli"), 14 (2013–14)
- Most wins: [Jonathan Quick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Quick "Jonathan Quick"), 16 (2011–12, 2013–14)
- Most shutouts: [Jonathan Quick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jonathan_Quick "Jonathan Quick"), 3 (2011–12, [2012–13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NHL_season "2012–13 NHL season"))

Team records

- Most points in a season: 105 ( [1974–75](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974%E2%80%9375_NHL_season "1974–75 NHL season"))
- Most wins in a season: 48 (2015–16)
- Longest regular season winning streak: 9 ( [2009–10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season "2009–10 NHL season"))
- Longest playoff winning streak: 8 (2011–12)

## Broadcasters

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Broadcasters")\]

Main article: [List of Los Angeles Kings broadcasters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Kings_broadcasters "List of Los Angeles Kings broadcasters")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Daryl_Evans.jpg/250px-Daryl_Evans.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Daryl_Evans.jpg) [Daryl Evans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daryl_Evans "Daryl Evans") is the Kings' current radio [color commentator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Color_commentator "Color commentator").

In 1973, the Kings hired [Bob Miller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Miller_(sports_announcer) "Bob Miller (sports announcer)") as their play-by-play announcer. Considered to be one of the finest hockey play-by-play announcers, Miller held the post continuously until retirement in 2017, and is often referred to as the _Voice of the Kings_. He received the Foster Hewitt Memorial Award from the NHL Hockey Broadcasters Association on November 13, 2000, making him a media honoree for the [Hockey Hall of Fame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hockey_Hall_of_Fame "Hockey Hall of Fame"),[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-FosHA-150)[\[153\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-0708MediaGuideP27-155) and he also earned a star in the [Hollywood Walk of Fame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame "Hollywood Walk of Fame") in 2006.[\[154\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-156) Miller has written two books about his experiences with the team, _Bob Miller's Tales of the Los Angeles Kings_ (2006),[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-MillerTales-157) and _Tales From The Los Angeles Kings Locker Room: A Collection Of The Greatest Kings Stories Ever Told_ (2013).[\[156\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-FR-Book2-158) On March 2, 2017, citing health reasons, Miller announced his retirement after 44 years with the team, and finished his career broadcasting the final two games of the 2016–17 Kings season.[\[157\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-MillerFinal2-159) The Kings named [NBCSN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBCSN "NBCSN") announcer [Alex Faust](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Faust "Alex Faust") as Miller's replacement, play-by-play announcer the team on TV for the [2017–18 season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_NHL_season "2017–18 NHL season") on June 1, 2017.[\[158\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-Faust-160)

On September 18, 2018. the team announced that it would cease over-the-air radio broadcasts, and had partnered with [iHeartMedia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IHeartMedia "IHeartMedia") to form the _Los Angeles Kings Audio Network_, which streams exclusively on the [iHeartRadio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IHeartRadio "IHeartRadio") platform. The deal also includes pre-game shows and other ancillary content streaming on iHeartRadio. Two pre-season games were simulcast by [KEIB](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KEIB "KEIB") before the transition was completed.[\[159\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-161)[\[160\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-162)

On June 5, 2023, the Kings parted ways with Alex Faust and planned on returning to a TV/radio simulcast format with [Nick Nickson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Nickson "Nick Nickson"), [Jim Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Fox_(ice_hockey) "Jim Fox (ice hockey)") and [Daryl Evans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daryl_Evans "Daryl Evans"), which they last used in the 1989–90 season.[\[161\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-163)

On September 14, 2023, the Kings announced a new contract with [Bally Sports West](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bally_Sports_West "Bally Sports West"), airing around 65 games, and [KCAL-TV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KCAL-TV "KCAL-TV"), airing around 6 games.[\[162\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-164)[\[163\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-165)

On June 20, 2024, the Kings announced a new deal with [ESPN Radio 710](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESPN_Radio_710 "ESPN Radio 710") to stream all games on the ESPN LA app, with 25 games to simulcast on the radio.[\[164\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-166)[\[165\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-167)

Nick Nickson retired after the 2024–25 season, and the Kings reverted to employing separate radio and television announce teams. On September 11, 2025, former [St. Louis Blues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis_Blues "St. Louis Blues") announcer [John Kelly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Kelly_(sportscaster) "John Kelly (sportscaster)") was hired to call games on television, while Josh Schaefer was promoted to lead play-by-play on radio. On games where Kelly was assigned to work nationally for [ESPN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NHL_on_ESPN "NHL on ESPN"), Schaefer would take over on television. Additionally, the Kings brought in former players [Ray Ferraro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Ferraro "Ray Ferraro"), [Tony Granato](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Granato "Tony Granato") and [Jarret Stoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jarret_Stoll "Jarret Stoll") to rotate alongside lead analyst Jim Fox on television.[\[166\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-168)[\[167\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-169)

On March 9, 2026, the [Los Angeles Angels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels "Los Angeles Angels") announced that they would acquire FanDuel Sports Network West from [Main Street Sports Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Main_Street_Sports_Group "Main Street Sports Group"),[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:2-170)[\[169\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:3-171) amid an expected winddown of the company's operations due to financial issues.[\[170\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-172)[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-173) The Angels also announced that they would renew the channel's rights to the Kings for the 2026–27 season,[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:2-170)[\[169\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-:3-171) In a transitional move, it was announced on March 18 that the remainder of the team's regional games for the season would air on now-former sister channel [FanDuel Sports Network SoCal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FanDuel_Sports_Network_SoCal "FanDuel Sports Network SoCal").[\[172\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-174)

**Television:** [FanDuel Sports Network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FanDuel_Sports_Network "FanDuel Sports Network") and [KCAL-TV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KCAL-TV "KCAL-TV")

- [John Kelly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Kelly_(sportscaster) "John Kelly (sportscaster)") – lead play-by-play
- [Jim Fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Fox_(ice_hockey) "Jim Fox (ice hockey)") – primary color commentator
- [Ray Ferraro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ray_Ferraro "Ray Ferraro") – backup color commentator
- [Tony Granato](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Granato "Tony Granato") – backup color commentator
- [Jarret Stoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jarret_Stoll "Jarret Stoll") – backup color commentator

**Radio:** [ESPN Radio 710](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESPN_Radio_710 "ESPN Radio 710") and ESPN LA App

- Josh Schaefer – lead radio play-by-play and backup television play-by-play
- [Daryl Evans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daryl_Evans "Daryl Evans") – color commentator
- Sam Betesh – Kings Talk co-host

**Public address:**

- David Courtney 1989–2012
- Dave Joseph 2013–2020[\[173\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-DaveJoseph-175)
- Trevor Rabone 2021–present

## Affiliate teams

\[ [edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Los_Angeles_Kings&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Affiliate teams")\]

The Kings are currently affiliated with the [Ontario Reign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ontario_Reign_(AHL) "Ontario Reign (AHL)") in the [American Hockey League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Hockey_League "American Hockey League"), they also have an affiliation with the [Greenville Swamp Rabbits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenville_Swamp_Rabbits "Greenville Swamp Rabbits") in the [ECHL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ECHL "ECHL"). Previous affiliates included the [Manchester Monarchs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_Monarchs_(AHL) "Manchester Monarchs (AHL)"), [Lowell Lock Monsters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lowell_Lock_Monsters "Lowell Lock Monsters"), [Springfield Falcons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Springfield_Falcons "Springfield Falcons"), [New Haven Nighthawks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Haven_Nighthawks "New Haven Nighthawks"), [Binghamton Dusters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binghamton_Dusters "Binghamton Dusters") and [Springfield Kings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Springfield_Indians "Springfield Indians") of the [AHL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Hockey_League "American Hockey League"); [Manchester Monarchs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_Monarchs_(ECHL) "Manchester Monarchs (ECHL)") and [Reading Royals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reading_Royals "Reading Royals") in the [ECHL](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ECHL "ECHL"); [Long Beach Ice Dogs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_Beach_Ice_Dogs "Long Beach Ice Dogs"), [Phoenix Roadrunners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoenix_Roadrunners_(IHL) "Phoenix Roadrunners (IHL)") and [Utah Grizzlies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah_Grizzlies_(1995%E2%80%932005) "Utah Grizzlies (1995–2005)") in the [International Hockey League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Hockey_League "International Hockey League"); and the [Houston Apollos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston_Apollos "Houston Apollos") of the [Central Hockey League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Professional_Hockey_League "Central Professional Hockey League").[\[174\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings#cite_note-176)
